2989

2990 </div>

2991

2992 </div>

2993

2994</div>

2995

2996<p>

2997<span style="font-weight: 400">

2998Visit a dog park in a state where cannabis is legal, and you’re sure to overhear someone recommend giving CBD to their pet. Similar to the way we talk about CBD and humans, there is a plethora of examples where CBD might help–anxiety when traveling or going to the vet, pain maintenance, using THC as a tumor inhibitor, etc. If you Google search “cbd and pets” right now, the results show three times the options of “pet-friendly” products to buy as there are educational resources. There is no question that people are already medicating their dogs with forms of cannabis and CBD extracts. </span>

2999</p>

3000

3001<div class="article_paragraph_2">

3002</div>

3003

3004<p>

3005Despite the rise in experimentation, there remains very little research on the subject. So the very big question remains: Is it safe to give cannabis to my pet?</p>

3006

3007<p>

3008<span style="font-weight: 400">

3009Part of the mystery around cannabis and animals is because of the fact cannabis is still federally illegal, so there hasn’t been funding or legal access to cannabis for potential projects. Without that research, the </span>

3010<a href="https://www.avma.org/KB/Resources/Reference/Pages/Cannabis-Use-Pets.aspx" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:https://www.avma.org/KB/Resources/Reference/Pages/Cannabis-Use-Pets.aspx" aria-label="American Veterinary Medical Association">

3011<span style="font-weight: 400" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:https://www.avma.org/KB/Resources/Reference/Pages/Cannabis-Use-Pets.aspx">

3012American Veterinary Medical Association</span>

3013</a>

3014<span style="font-weight: 400">

3015 can’t state that vets are allowed to even discuss cannabis as a possible recommended medication without risking their medical license. That being said, they released </span>

3016<a href="http://news.vin.com/apputil/image/handler.ashx?docid=8473679" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:http://news.vin.com/apputil/image/handler.ashx?docid=8473679" aria-label="a document">

3017<span style="font-weight: 400" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:http://news.vin.com/apputil/image/handler.ashx?docid=8473679">

3018a document</span>

3019</a>

3020<span style="font-weight: 400">

3021 to members in February of this year titled “Cannabis: What Veterinarians Need to Know” to help doctors “advise clients and treat patients who may have been exposed to marijuana.”</span>

3022</p>

3023

3024<p>

3025<span style="font-weight: 400">

3026The document gives a cursory breakdown of cannabis, cannabinoids like THC and CBD, concentrates and high-CBD/low-THC hemp plants, but only provides recommendations based on results from cases where animals came in to the vet from a toxic reaction. The evidence shows your animal will typically experience effects within 1-3 hours of exposure, but that they can “manifest in as little as 5 minutes or as long as 96 hours.” The AVMA notice also explains that most toxic cases have occurred in young puppies, and that most cases with dogs involved other toxicities such as chocolate, raisins, xylitol or wrapping. </span>

3027</p>

3028

3029<div class="vestpocket" vest-pocket>

3030</div>

3031

3032<div id="attachment_116" class="wp-caption wp-caption-wrap alignnone">

3033

3034 <div class="article-body-image image-embed__placeholder" style="padding-top: 74.96%; position: relative;">

3035

3036 <progressive-image class="size-large wp-image-116" src="https://blogs-images.forbes.com/laurenterry/files/2018/09/IMG_3649-1200x900.jpg" alt="Remember to be lighthanded–you're seeking to provide relief to your pet, not sedation." data-height="900" data-width="1200">

3037</progressive-image>

3038

3039 </div>

3040

3041 <div class="article-image-caption">

3042

3043 <div class="caption-container" ng-class="caption_state">

3044

3045 <fbs-accordion>

3046

3047 <p class="wp-caption-text" aria-hidden="true">

3048Remember to be lighthanded–you're seeking to provide relief to your pet, not sedation.</p>

3049

3050 <small class="article-photo-credit">

3051Lauren Yoshiko</small>

3052

3053 </fbs-accordion>

3054

3055 </div>

3056

3057 </div>

3058

3059</div>

3060

3061<fbs-ad position="inread" progressive ad-id="article-0-inread" aria-hidden="true" role="presentation">

3062</fbs-ad>

3063

3064<p>

3065<span style="font-weight: 400">

3066Ultimately, it states that due to federal regulations, cbd oil or chews, “despite contrary claims,” are illegal for use in pets. But there is no acknowledgement of evidence that shows a toxic effect from CBD extract. As with everything we put in our, and our pets’, bodies, it comes down to proper dosage.</span>

3067</p>

3068

3069<p>

3070<span style="font-weight: 400">

3071Dr. Cornelia Wagner, owner of </span>

3072<a href="http://hawthornevet.com/resources/medicinal-cannabis-pets" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:http://hawthornevet.com/resources/medicinal-cannabis-pets" aria-label="Hawthorne Veterinary Clinic">

3073<span style="font-weight: 400" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:http://hawthornevet.com/resources/medicinal-cannabis-pets">

3074Hawthorne Veterinary Clinic</span>

3075</a>

3076<span style="font-weight: 400">

3077 in Portland, OR, is one of the veterinarians opening her mind and her doctor’s office to the idea of cannabis as a safe, effective medicine when dosed properly. She’s the first to acknowledge that there are no clear medical guidelines for doing so, and thus strictly recommends beginning any pet’s treatment with the lowest amount possible–about 1 mg/ml a day.</span>

3078</p>

3079

3080<div class="article_paragraph_7">

3081</div>

3082

3083<p>

3084<i>

3085<span style="font-weight: 400">

3086“</span>

3087</i>

3088<span style="font-weight: 400">

3089The upper dose limit for CBD products recommended is around 1 mg/kg/day orally, but one should start with a much smaller fraction of this dose such as 0.05 mg/kg/day,” states Dr. Wagner on the Hawthorne Clinic’s website. “For THC products, start with an oral dose of 0.1-0.25 mg/kg THC once or twice daily.”</span>

3090</p>

3091

3092<p>

3093<span style="font-weight: 400">

3094If you don’t see any negative side effects (excessive sedation, disorientation, excitement, vomiting, etc.), Wagner states that the pet has developed a tolerance and the dose can be gradually increased every 5 days or so until the desired effect is seen. Stick to increases no larger than .05ml/mg &nbsp;a week.</span>

3095</p>

3096

3097<p>

3098<span style="font-weight: 400">

3099One of the reasons the THC dosage should be administered with an even lighter hand is because dogs have a more complex endocannabinoid system as humans, with many more receptors. They feel the effects of THC much stronger than we do. Although infused dog treats are available at most dispensaries, pet-owners who keep cannabis tincture around can use that as well, just in smaller amounts. There are options like a whole plant-extract&nbsp;formula by <a href="https://www.luminousbotanicals.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:https://www.luminousbotanicals.com/" aria-label="Luminous Botanicals">

3100Luminous Botanicals</a>

3101&nbsp;at Oregon dispensaries,&nbsp;or this <a href="http://www.groncbd.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:http://www.groncbd.com" aria-label="GrönCBD">

3102GrönCBD</a>

3103&nbsp;tincture–an example of safe, synthetic CBD made from tree lichen. To achieve these small doses, you can use a water syringe to separate the proper sized dose and then some water, so it can be squirted quickly and directly into your pet’s mouth.</span>

3104</p>

3105

3106<div id="attachment_117" class="wp-caption wp-caption-wrap alignnone">

3107

3108 <div class="article-body-image image-embed__placeholder" style="padding-top: 74.96%; position: relative;">

3109

3110 <progressive-image class="size-full wp-image-117" src="https://blogs-images.forbes.com/laurenterry/files/2018/09/IMG_3643.jpg" alt="Happy boys, happy house." data-height="768" data-width="1024">

3111</progressive-image>

3112

3113 </div>

3114

3115 <div class="article-image-caption">

3116

3117 <div class="caption-container" ng-class="caption_state">

3118

3119 <fbs-accordion>

3120

3121 <p class="wp-caption-text" aria-hidden="true">

3122Happy boys, happy house.</p>

3123

3124 <small class="article-photo-credit">

3125Lauren Yoshiko</small>

3126

3127 </fbs-accordion>

3128

3129 </div>

3130

3131 </div>

3132

3133</div>

3134

3135<p>

3136<span style="font-weight: 400">

3137Fortunately for cannabis-curious pet-owners, the spread of legalization across the country is giving doctors enough resources (nerve) to take research into their own hands. In Colorado, Dr. Stephanie McGrath, a neurologist and assistant professor at Colorado State University's College of Veterinary Medicine &amp; Biomedical Sciences, </span>

3138<a href="https://www.avma.org/News/JAVMANews/Pages/180801a.aspx" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:https://www.avma.org/News/JAVMANews/Pages/180801a.aspx" aria-label="has completed">

3139<span style="font-weight: 400" data-ga-track="ExternalLink:https://www.avma.org/News/JAVMANews/Pages/180801a.aspx">

3140has completed</span>

3141</a>

3142<span style="font-weight: 400">

3143 two clinical studies since 2016 on the effects of cannabidiol in dogs with osteoarthritis or epilepsy. In</span>

3144 <span style="font-weight: 400">

3145January, the American Kennel Club granted Dr. McGrath $350,000 for her to begin a three-year crossover study of CBD for epilepsy in dogs. Legislation has been proposed in New York and California that would establish guidelines and allow veterinarians to legally discuss the use of cannabis products with their clients. </span>

3146</p>

3147

3148<p>

3149<span style="font-weight: 400">

3150Until then, when you go shopping for tincture or “pet-friendly” cannabis or hemp products, just don’t hold back when asking about ingredient sources, any available testing on the cannabis material, and where it was grown/produced. This intersection of the FDA, the DEA, conflicting state laws and the equally-conflicted veterinary community means that a lot of medical claims and questionable synthetic formulas have been thrown around recklessly. We all just want our pets to feel good–make sure they’re getting the real deal.</span>

3151</p>

3152

3179<div class="contributor-about__initial-description">

3180<p class="author-description">

3181A West Coast native with the ability to smell a legitimate cut of Girl Scout Cookies and a Literature degree from the University of California at Santa Cruz, Lauren was…</p>

3182<button class="toggle-description contributor-about__read-more" data-vars-event-label="contrib block expand" data-ga-track="contrib block expand">

3183&nbsp;Read More</button>

3184</div>

3185<div class="contributor-about__full-description contributor-about__description-hidden">

3186<p class="author-description">

3187A West Coast native with the ability to smell a legitimate cut of Girl Scout Cookies and a Literature degree from the University of California at Santa Cruz, Lauren was destined to be a cannabis culture critic. Since moving to Portland in 2013, she's experienced working for a dispensary, running one, managing harvest and sales at a state-licensed farm, all the while writing about the legal updates, plant science, consumer trends and the emerging scene around social consumption. Her articles about the cultural and commercial happenings in the cannabis industry have appeared in Willamette Week, Broccoli, High Times and Rolling Stone, among others.</p>
